__label__good__label__Does the argument that, If a person is old enough to fight and die for their country, they are old enough to do x. annoy you as much as it does me? 
__label__good__label__You know, as cliche as it is, I can't actually find much cause to disagree with that statement.  Usually, though, I think the statement is used to say that the age of majority for some activity should be lowered to 18 (usually drinking - occasionally, renting a car or somesuch), whereas I tend to view it as a better argument for RAISING the age of majority for military recruitment.  If society thinks someone is still a little too irresponsible to be trusted with weak depressants that can carry medical risks in large quantities, why do we think the same person can be trusted to sign up to kill and die for a GI bill or some sense of patriotism?

__label__good__label__The gay rights 'agenda,' from what I understand, is nothing more than to get equal partnership rights to straights.  Which is to say, to get discriminatory laws stricken from the books that treat gay couples differently from (worse than) straight couples, or that don't recognize them at all.  I've kept an open mind for good arguments against this for a long time, and I have yet to be presented with a convincing reason that gays shouldn't have equal rights, with regard to marriage, adoption, taxation, serving in the military, and everywhere else they're discriminated against.
